Article 450.27 Oil-Insulated Transformers Installed Outdoors. Amend to read as
follows:
Space separations shall be no less than five (5) feet horizontally from a
doorway or window and twenty (20) feet from a fire escape except with written
permission of the fire code official or his/her designee.
Article 525.20(G) Protection. Amend to read as follows:
Flexible cords and cables running on the ground where accessible to the public
shall be covered with approved nonconductive mats. Cables and mats shall be
arranged so as not to present a tripping hazard.
Article 600.6(A) Sign Disconnects. Amend to read as follows:
Outdoor disconnects and raceways used in connection with illuminated signage
shall be located in accordance with one of the following methods:
      1.   Within an enclosed building within sight of the sign(s), or
      2.   Behind a parapet wall within sight of the sign(s), or
      3.   Completely enclosed within the sign.
Article 604 Manufactured Wiring Systems. Amend to read as follows:
Manufactured wiring systems shall be permitted for use with furniture systems
only.
Article 680.23(A)(4) Voltage Limitation. Amend to read as follows:
Lighting fixtures installed in swimming pools, fountains, and the like, shall
not operate at more than 15 volts, as measured between conductors.
Article 720 Low Voltage Wiring. Amend by adding the following:
Low voltage wiring shall be installed in conduit in areas made inaccessible by
building construction or where subject to damage.
      3.   Appendix 3:
   Amendments To 2006 Edition
   Of The International Fire Code
The 2006 edition of the international fire code as adopted is amended as
follows:
Section 101.1 Title. Amend to read as follows:
These regulations shall be known as the fire code of the village of Golf,
hereinafter referred to as "this code."
Section 102.6 Referenced Codes And Standards. Amend to read as follows:
The codes and standards referenced in this code shall be those that are listed
in chapter 45 and such codes and standards shall be considered part of the
requirements of this code to the prescribed extent of each such reference.
Where differences occur between the provisions of this code and the referenced
standards, the provisions of this code shall apply. The following codes and
standards are not adopted by reference:
IPC-2006 international plumbing code;
IWUIC-2006 international wildland-urban interface code.
Section 505.1 Address Numbers. Amend to read as follows:
Each structure to which an address number has been assigned shall have such
number displayed in compliance with the Golf village code.
Section 506.1 Key Boxes. Amend to read as follows:
All buildings or structures equipped with a fire alarm or fire suppression
system shall provide a fire department key box on the exterior of the building
or structure. The box shall contain keys to allow fire department entry in the
event of fire alarm activation or an emergency. The fire official may also
require a fire department key box if access to the building, structure or area
is unduly difficult. All fire department key boxes, location of the key boxes,
and the number of key boxes required shall be approved by the fire official.
Section 903.2.7 Group R. Delete this section.
Section 903.3.5 Water Supplies. Amend to read as follows:
Water supplies for automatic sprinkler systems shall comply with this section
and the standards referenced in section 903.3.1. The potable water supply shall
be protected against backflow in accordance with the requirements of this
section and the adopted plumbing code. Hydrant flow data used for the design of
any sprinkler system shall be no more than one (1) year old.
Section 903.3.5.3 Low Water Pressure Factor. Amend by adding this section:
Provide a minimum 10%, but not less than 5 psi, safety factor in the fire
protection system hydraulic calculation. The system demand shall be a minimum 5
psi below the annual water flow test supply.
Section 903.4.2.1 Additional Alarm Location. Amend by adding the following:
An approved alarm notification appliance (audio/visual device) shall be
provided on the exterior of the building or structure and located over the fire
department connection or as approved by the authority having jurisdiction.
Section 903.4.2.2 Location. Amend by adding this section:
Alarm notification appliances and approved audio/visual devices shall be
provided and located per NFPA 72.
Section 903.4.3 Floor Control Valves. Amend to read as follows:
Approved supervised indicating control valves shall be provided at the point of
connection to the riser on each floor of the building or structure.
Section 903.4.4 Additional Smoke Detectors Required. Amend by adding this
section:
Where automatic sprinkler system provides protection to an area with an
approved flow switch interconnected to the fire alarm system, and the area is
easily identifiable as to the location of the activation, additional automatic
detectors are not required. When a building has numerous rooms protected by the
zoned sprinkler system, the authority having jurisdiction may require
additional smoke detectors.
Section 903.5.1 Accessibility. Amend by adding this section:
Fire sprinkler systems inspection test valves shall be accessible at all times
and located no more than 6' above the finished floor surface. On multiple riser
systems test valves shall be clearly identified in permanent marking as to the
riser and area served.
Section 903.7 Referenced Standards. Amend by adding this section:
All references to NFPA standards are to be considered part of this code.
Exceptions:
NFPA 101 life safety code
NFPA 5000 building code
Section 903.8 Fire Pump Test Header. Amend by adding this section:
Automatic sprinkler systems that are equipped with an approved fire pump shall
be provided with an OS&Y (or approved equal) control valve on the fire pump
test header(s). Fire pump installations shall include an exterior test header.
Section 903.9 Private Fire Hydrants: Amend by adding this section:
In developed lots, subdivisions or parcels, fire hydrants shall be located in
that no fire hydrant is located no greater than 300' from nearest fire hydrant.
Fire hydrants shall be provided on all sides of a developed lot, subdivision or
parcel as approved by the authority having jurisdiction. One (1) fire hydrant
shall be located not more than 100' of the fire department connection on the
fire protection water supply to the building or structure.
Section 903.10 Fire Department Access. Amend by adding this section:
Rooms or spaces containing an automatic sprinkler system riser valve and/or a
fire pump shall be provided with direct access from the exterior of the
building or structure.
Section 903.11 Warehouse Storage. Delete this section.
Section 903.12 Backflow Protection. Amend by adding this section:
Backflow protection shall be provided on automatic sprinkler system risers in
S1 and S2 occupancies that have a floor area greater than 20,000 square feet
and storage in excess of 12' in height.
Section 906.1 Portable Fire Extinguishers. Amend to read as follows:
Where required: A portable fire extinguisher shall be installed in the
following locations in accordance with NFPA 10, 2007 edition.
      1.   In all occupancies in use groups A-1, A-2, A-3, A-4, B, F-1, F-2, I-
1, M, R-1 (except single family dwellings not used as adult care or child care
facilities), S-1, S-2, and H.
      2.   In all areas containing commercial kitchen exhaust hood systems
class K fire extinguishers are required.
      3.   In all areas where fuel is used, stored or dispensed.
      4.   In all areas where flammable or combustible liquids is used in the
operation of spraying, coating, or dipping.
      5.   In all occupancies in use group I-3 at staff locations. Access to
portable fire extinguishers shall be permitted to be locked.
      6.   On each floor of structures under construction, except occupancies
in use group R-3.
      7.   In any laboratory, shop or other room of similar purpose.
      8.   Where required by sections indicated in table 906.1 for various
operations, processes, structures and areas.
Section 907.1.2 Equipment. Amend to read as follows:
Systems and their components shall be listed and approved for the purpose for
which they are installed. Systems shall be installed per NFPA 72.
Section 907.2 Where Required - New Buildings And Structures. Delete this
section in its entirety.
Section 907.2.2 Automatic Fire Detection System Required. Amend by adding this
section:
An approved automatic fire detection system shall be installed in all use
groups, not provided with an automatic sprinkler system, and in accordance with
NFPA 72. Devices, combination of devices, appliances, and equipment shall
comply with section 907.1.2. The automatic fire detectors shall be smoke
detectors, except that an approved alternative type of detector shall be
installed in spaces such as boiler rooms where during normal operation products
of combustion are present in sufficient quantity to activate a smoke detector.
Section 907.2.3 Control Panel Locations. Amend by adding this section:
All fire alarm control panels or full function annunciators panels shall be
installed within 10 feet of the main entrance, or in a location approved by the
fire department.
Section 907.11 Fire Safety Functions. Amend by adding this section:
Automatic fire detectors utilized for the purpose of performing fire safety
functions shall be connected to the building's fire alarm control panel where a
fire alarm system is required by section 907.2. Detectors shall, upon
actuation, perform the intended function and activate the alarm notification
appliances or a visible and audible supervisory signal at a constantly attended
location. In buildings not required to be equipped with a fire alarm system,
the automatic fire detector shall be powered by normal electric service and,
upon actuation, perform the intended function. The detectors shall be located
in accordance with chapter 5 of NFPA 72. Multi-tenant group M buildings will be
activated by individual tenant space by the automatic sprinkler system flow
switch for that space or an automatic fire detection system.
Section 912.1.1 Fire Department Connections. Amend by adding this section:
All fire department connection shall be a NST, 4 inch Storz connection with a
30 degree down turn.
Section 1006.3.1 Additional Illumination Requirements. Amend by adding this
section:
All rooms containing the building fire sprinkler riser(s), fire pump(s) and
fire alarm control panel(s) shall be provided with approved emergency lighting.
Section 3301.1.3 Fireworks. Amend to read as follows:
The possession, manufacture, storage, sale, handling and use of fireworks are
prohibited.
Exceptions:
            (1)   Storage and handling and use of fireworks at display sites in
accordance with sections 3304 and 3308.5 and NFPA 1123 or NFPA 1126 listed in
chapter 35 of the 2006 international building code.
            (2)   The retail sale of approved consumer novelties as defined by
this ordinance shall be permitted but only to persons 18 years of age or older
shall be permitted only in buildings equipped with approved automatic sprinkler
systems. The display of consumer novelties in a building shall be separated
from all exit doors by a minimum distance of 20 feet or as approved in advance
in writing by the fire chief. The sale of consumer novelties shall not be
permitted at any building or on any property where flammable or combustible
liquids or gases are sold or dispensed.
Section 3301.1.3.1 Penalties For Possession. Amend by adding this section:
Any person, firm, corporation, or entity that violates any provision of section
3301.1.3 shall be subject to an escalating fine schedule as follows:
      1.   First offense: $50.
      2.   Second offense: $100.
      3.   Third offense and each subsequent offense: $250.
Section 3302.1 Definitions. Amend by adding the following:
Consumer novelties. Consumer novelties shall mean: (i) snakes, glow worm
pellets, smoke devices, trick snappers, trick matches, cigarette loads, auto
burglar alarms, toy pistols, toy canes, toy guns, and other devices in which
paper or plastic caps containing 0.25 grains or less of explosive compound are
used, provided they are constructed so that the hand cannot come in contact
with the cap when in place for the explosion, and (ii) toy pistol paper or
plastic caps which contain less than 0.25 grains of explosive mixture.
Section 3308.2.1 Outdoor Displays. Amend to read as follows:
In addition to the requirements of section 403, permit applications for outdoor
fireworks displays using division 1.3G fireworks shall include a diagram of the
location at which the display will be conducted, including the site from which
fireworks will be discharged; the location of buildings, highways, overhead
obstructions and utilities; and the lines behind which the audience will be
restrained. All outdoor fireworks displays shall be electronically fired using
approved electronic firing units and approved mortar racks. All outdoor
fireworks displays shall comply with the provisions of the Illinois pyrotechnic
use act (425 ILCS 35), and the pyrotechnic distributor and operator licensing
act (225 ILCS 227).
Section 3308.11 Retail Display And Sale. Amend to read as follows:
It shall be unlawful to display, sell, store, or advertise for sale any class
1.3G or 1.4G fireworks within the village of Golf.
(Ord. 2009-17, 11-9-2009)
      4.   Appendix 4:
   Amendments To Illinois Plumbing Code
The Illinois plumbing code is adopted with the following amendment:
Pursuant to 17 Ill. admin. code 3730.307(c)(4) and subject to the Illinois
plumbing code (77 Ill. admin. code 890) and the lawn irrigation contractor and
lawn sprinkler system registration code (77 Ill. admin. code 892), all new
plumbing fixtures and irrigation controllers installed after November 9, 2015
shall bear the WaterSense label (as designated by the U.S. environmental
protection agency WaterSense program), when such labeled fixtures are
available.
(Ord. 2016-01, 1-11-2016)
8-1-3: BUILDING PERMITS; DUTIES OF BUILDING COMMISSIONER:
   A.   Permit Required: No building or other structure shall be constructed,
remodeled, repaired, moved or demolished where the cost of such construction,
remodeling, repairing, moving or demolition is in excess of one thousand
dollars ($1,000.00) unless a building permit authorizing such construction,
remodeling, repairing, moving or demolition shall first have been procured from
the building commissioner.
   B.   Application For Permit: Permits for constructing, remodeling,
repairing, moving or demolishing a building or buildings, or other structures,
shall be procured by making application for same by submitting a building
permit application to the building commissioner. No application shall be
accepted unless signed by the owner of the property to which the application
relates, or by his duly authorized agent. Applications shall be made only on
forms furnished by the building commissioner. Each application shall be
accompanied by the submissions required in chapter 3 of this title. Plans and
specifications for construction of new buildings, additions to existing
buildings or other structures shall be certified by a licensed architect.
   C.   Issuance Of Permit: No building permit shall be issued if site
preparation work has not been completed in accordance with the requirements of
any site preparation permit issued as a preliminary condition to performing the
work. However, if the application is in proper form and if it appears therefrom
and from the plans and specifications submitted with such application that the
work proposed to be undertaken does conform with this title and all other
village ordinances, and when all site preparation work has been performed and
the required fees, charges and deposits are made, the building commissioner
shall issue the building permit applied for.
   D.   Water Connection Fee: The water connection fee is provided for in
section
7-1-5 of this code.
   E.   Duties Of Building Commissioner: The building commissioner shall have
the powers and duties assigned to the position of building commissioner as set
forth in this title. Whenever any of the adopted codes refer to "administrative
authority" or "code official", such terms shall refer to the building
commissioner. Any person serving as building commissioner shall have a broad
knowledge of building construction insofar as practical and technical concepts
including the related fields of plumbing, heating, ventilating and electrical
construction. The building commissioner's basic duties shall be as follows:
      1.   Set up, keep and maintain a file of applications, permits issued,
plats diagrams, plans and other data required by this title to be filed.
      2.   Receive all applications for building permits and approve the
issuance of building permits when the applications comply with the requirements
of this title.
      3.   Receive reports of inspectors of the village of Golf or other
recognized inspection services, after investigation of their qualifications and
reliability, in connection with reviews of commercial projects or code matters
beyond the general competence of the building commissioner, provided such
reports shall be made in writing and certified by a responsible person of such
agency or service.
      4.   Make the necessary practical inspections of work performed in the
field or reasonably ascertain whether all regulations of this title to
property, buildings or structures are complied with.
      5.   Keep a record of all inspections made, of reports rendered and of
notices of orders issued and deposit such records in the individual property
file previously mentioned. (Ord. 2009-17, 11-9-2009)
8-1-4: CERTIFICATE OF OCCUPANCY:
Upon the completion of any new construction or remodeling, the building
commissioner shall issue to the owner of the property a certificate of
occupancy, subject to the finding by the building commissioner that such new
construction or remodeling complies with all the provisions of this title and
the village zoning ordinance 1 . (Ord. 2009-17, 11-9-2009)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 9 of this code.
8-1-5: FEES, CHARGES AND DEPOSITS:
Permit and inspection fees shall be as set forth in the annual fee schedule in
effect at the time a permit application is submitted, as adopted by the board
of trustees pursuant to this code, including all amendments thereto. (Ord.
2009-17, 11-9-2009)
8-1-6: PERMIT TIME LIMITS:
No permit or approval made pursuant to the village building code shall be valid
for a period of more than one year after the date of issuance. An extension of
time may be granted by the village upon request, provided, however that no such
extension shall exceed eighteen (18) months from the original date of issuance
of the permit. Permits for fences, driveways and smaller projects when issued
may be initially valid only for six (6) months as appropriate for the project.
(Ord. 2009-17, 11-9-2009)
8-1-7: PLUMBING REGULATIONS IN BASEMENTS:
   A.   All new buildings with basements, floors, rooms or occupancy areas
below ground level at the building site and served by a public or private sewer
system, shall have overhead plumbing. No building permit application will be
accepted nor any permits issued for construction of any structure unless plans
and specifications therefor provide for overhead plumbing as called for in this
section.
   B.   Footing drains shall be connected to sump pumps for further discharge
into drainage ditches or approved drainage conveyance system. No footing drain
or drainage tile shall be connected to the sanitary sewer system. (Ord. 2009-
17, 11-9-2009)
8-1-8: PENALTIES:
Any person violating any provisions of this chapter shall be subject to a class
D penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 2009-17, 11-9-2009)
CHAPTER 2
ARCHITECTURAL DESIGN
SECTION:
8-2-1: Building Assistance Committee Created
8-2-2: Architectural Design Conformance
8-2-3: Design Review
8-2-4: Committee Review And Appeal
8-2-5: Violations And Penalties
8-2-1: BUILDING ASSISTANCE COMMITTEE CREATED:
There is hereby created a building assistance committee for the village. The
members of the committee are the village architect, the building commissioner
and the building inspector. Should one person fill both the building
commissioner and the building inspector positions, then the village president
may appoint a third member to the committee at his or her discretion. (Ord. 08-
07, 8-13-2007)
8-2-2: ARCHITECTURAL DESIGN CONFORMANCE:
Every building hereafter constructed, erected, altered or enlarged in the
village shall be so designed and constructed as to be architecturally suitable
to its environment and shall not be incompatible or incongruous with the
exterior design and appearance of buildings constructed or in the course of
construction in the neighborhood thereof. The building shall also be in
conformance with applicable provisions of the zoning regulations of this code 1
. (Ord. 00-03, 5-8-2000)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 9 of this code.
8-2-3: DESIGN REVIEW:
   A.   New Construction: Plans for all construction of all totally and
completely new buildings, shall be submitted to the building assistance
committee for review after the building commissioner has determined compliance
with all other ordinances of the village.
   B.   Existing Buildings: Whenever an application is filed with the building
commissioner for a building permit, and the building commissioner finds that
said application, plans and specifications and plot plans submitted therewith
otherwise comply with all the ordinances of the village, but that said
application provides for an addition to an existing structure, the exterior
design and appearance of which, in the opinion of the building commissioner,
may be incompatible or incongruous with the exterior design and appearance of
buildings constructed or in the course of construction in the neighborhood, or
is incompatible with the provisions of the zoning ordinance, the building
commissioner shall withhold the granting of such permit and shall, within
fifteen (15) days after receipt of the application file said application
together with his written and signed opinion with the members of the building
assistance committee for review by said committee. (Ord. 00-03, 5-8-2000; amd.
2003 Code)
8-2-4: COMMITTEE REVIEW AND APPEAL:
The building assistance committee shall notify its members and applicant and
schedule a meeting within ten (10) working days following notification by the
building commissioner. The committee shall meet with the applicant and/or his
representatives to resolve any such issues as may be in conflict with village
code provisions, or incompatible or incongruous with the exterior design and
appearance of other buildings constructed or in the course of construction in
the neighborhood. If the issues are resolved, revised plans shall be submitted
to the building commissioner for further processing leading to the issuance of
a building permit. If the issues are not resolved, the applicant may appeal to
the village board. If the village board determines that there are potential
violations of the zoning ordinance, they shall direct a formal hearing before
the zoning board. If the village board finds that the issue is incompatibility
or incongruity with the exterior design and appearance of other buildings, the
village board shall make the final determination of the matter. (Ord. 00-03, 5-
8-2000)
8-2-5: VIOLATIONS AND PENALTIES:
Any person violating any provisions of this chapter shall be subject to a class
B penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 00-03, 5-8-2000)
CHAPTER 3
CONSTRUCTION AND DEMOLITION REGULATIONS
SECTION:
8-3-1: Applicability And Interpretation
8-3-2: Definitions
8-3-3: Street Restoration And Security
8-3-4: Required Plans And Specifications
8-3-5: Additional Required Plans And Standards
8-3-6: Site Management Standards
8-3-7: Commencement Of Demolition Or Construction
8-3-8: Penalties
8-3-1: APPLICABILITY AND INTERPRETATION:
   A.   Applicability: The standards and conditions set out in this chapter
shall apply to all work undertaken in the village in conjunction with a permit
issued under the building code of the village 1 . The provisions of this
chapter shall apply to every application for a permit filed on or after the
effective date hereof. In addition, the provisions of this chapter shall apply
to every pending application for a permit, regardless of when that application
was filed, and to every permit issued pursuant to the village building code,
regardless of when that permit was issued.
   B.   Interpretation: The requirements of this chapter shall apply to all
work, whether demolition work or construction work, for which a permit is
required under the building code of the village.
   C.   Inconsistency With Other Codes And Ordinances: In the event of any
inconsistency or conflict in the application or operation of the provisions of
this chapter and other provisions of the building code of the village, the
provisions of this chapter shall apply and control.
   D.   Administrative Rules And Regulations: The building commissioner shall
promulgate such administrative rules and regulations as may be necessary or
appropriate to carry out the purposes and intents of this chapter. (Ord. 02-03,
5-13-2002)
 
Notes
1 1. See section
  8-1-2 of this title.
8-3-2: DEFINITIONS:
For purposes of this chapter, the following terms are hereby adopted:
COMMENCEMENT OF CONSTRUCTION: The beginning of any work under permit for the
structure being constructed.
COMMENCEMENT OF DEMOLITION: Any work done in conjunction with a permit issued
pursuant to the village building code, other than the installation of the
protective fencing required pursuant to other code provisions and any approved
soil sedimentation and erosion control.
COMPLETION OF DEMOLITION: Removal of the walls of the first floor above the
foundation of the structure being demolished or removal of all foundation
material from the excavation in the case of a foundation removal.
CONSTRUCTION: All the on site work done in building or altering structures from
land clearance to completion, including excavation, erection and the assembly
and installation of components and equipment.
DEMOLITION: Where a permit to raze a structure or part thereof is required, the
razing and removal of all or substantially all of a structure or the removal of
such portions of a principal structure as to make the structure uninhabitable
or unsafe for human occupancy. (Ord. 02-03, 5-13-2002)
8-3-3: STREET RESTORATION AND SECURITY:
Prior to the issuance of any site preparation permit or building permit, the
applicant shall schedule a video and photographic inspection of the adjoining
streets and parkways to be conducted by the building department, which shall
prepare a dated VHS videotape or digital video disk (DVD) clearly showing the
existing condition of all portions of the street(s), shoulders, parkways,
ditches, and culverts along or within one hundred feet (100') of the property
to be developed (i.e., along the entire lot line adjoining the street and
extending from each end of such lot line for a distance of 100 feet along the
public or private street right of way beyond the boundary of the lot), and such
VHS videotape or DVD inspection report shall be admissible as sufficient
evidence in any court proceeding or other dispute between the applicant and the
village concerning the condition of such public or private street and nearby
parkways, ditches, and culverts prior to the applicant's activities. Prior to
the issuance of a building permit, site preparation permit, or site development
permit, the applicant shall also deliver to the village a form of security
herein described (the "street restoration security") to run to the benefit of
the village to protect the village and hold it free and harmless from all
claims or rights of action arising from or claimed to be due from the use of
said street, and for the further purpose of guaranteeing the restoration of
such street or streets or parkways in the event of any damage or injury caused
by such construction vehicles. The street restoration security shall consist of
either: a) a refundable cash deposit or b) an irrevocable, unconditional letter
of credit in a form satisfactory to the village. The street restoration
security may be posted by the owner of the property or the owner's contractor,
as the permit applicant, but in any event only one street restoration security
shall be required for a single construction project. A permit applicant
applying for permits for different construction projects on the same street
shall be required to furnish one street restoration security for each
construction project. The amount of the street restoration security shall be as
set forth in the annual fee schedule. Upon the faithful performance of the
conditions and provisions of the permits, the plans accompanying such permits
and other applicable provisions of this code, the cash deposit or letter of
credit shall be returned within thirty (30) days to the applicant. If there
shall be any damage to the adjoining streets used during the applicant's
construction, based upon a comparison of the video and photographic inspection
conducted by the building department, then the applicant's activities shall be
presumed to be the primary cause of such damage and the village may use the
street restoration security to restore the condition of the damaged street.
(Ord. 2009-17, 11-9-2009)
8-3-4: REQUIRED PLANS AND SPECIFICATIONS:
Every application for a permit shall be accompanied by the following plans and
specifications:
   A.   Building Plans And Specifications:
      1.   If the application includes demolition of a principal structure,
then the application shall include building plans and specifications prepared
in compliance with the provisions of the building code, for any structure to be
built on the subject property.
      2.   If commencement of construction of such structure is not planned to
occur, or does not occur within thirty (30) days after completion of
demolition, then the application also shall include a detailed site restoration
plan as provided in subsection B of this section.
   B.   Site Restoration Plans And Specifications: If the application includes
demolition of a principal structure and if commencement of construction of a
new structure is not planned to occur, or does not occur within thirty (30)
days after completion of demolition, then the application shall include a
detailed site restoration plan depicting all work required to restore the
subject property, within thirty (30) days after completion of demolition, to a
safe, clean condition until construction of a new structure has commenced,
including, without limitation, backfilling of any excavation, grading, seeding,
fencing, stormwater management and the like. (Ord. 02-03, 5-13-2002)
8-3-5: ADDITIONAL REQUIRED PLANS AND STANDARDS:
   A.   Stormwater Management And Soil Sedimentation And Erosion Control Plans:
In addition to all other village regulations, village ordinances, plans and
specifications, the application shall include detailed plans and specifications
for stormwater management, soil sedimentation and erosion control and grading
on the subject property. Such plans and specifications shall be on a drawing or
drawings separate from all other plans and specifications, labeled as
stormwater management plans and/or soil sedimentation and erosion control
plans. Such plans and specifications shall be prepared and certified by a
professional engineer, shall be made in conformance with the requirements of
the village and shall include a certification by the applicant, in a form
provided by the village, that all requirements of the village's codes,
ordinances and regulations relating to stormwater management, soil erosion
control and grading shall be satisfied by the applicant at all times. Among
other details, the required stormwater management plans shall include:
      1.   Drainage plans and soil erosion control during demolition, if any.
      2.   Stormwater management and soil sedimentation and erosion control
during any period of time between completion of demolition and commencement of
construction.
      3.   Stormwater management and soil sedimentation and erosion control
commencing with preparation for foundation pouring and continuing during the
entire construction process until final grading of the subject property.
   B.   Accessibility, Parking And Loading Plans: The application shall include
separate plans and specifications showing the location of all work affecting,
and all parking and loading activities planned to take place on public streets,
sidewalks and other rights of way. Such plans and specifications shall include,
among other things, the location of pavement, sidewalk and trees that may be
affected by the proposed work; the impacts on such pavement, sidewalk and
trees; the proposed location for all parking of contractor and worker vehicles;
the proposed location of any loading or unloading activities including concrete
to occur within any right of way.
   C.   Materials And Spoils Storage Plans: The application shall include plans
depicting the proposed location for storage of materials and spoil on the
subject property that are consistent with village soil sedimentation and
erosion control requirements.
   D.   Dust And Airborne Particulate Control Provisions: The application shall
include provisions for controlling dust and other airborne particles from the
subject property, including, without limitation, a source of water and spraying
equipment and any other measures to be taken to control airborne particles.
   E.   Fencing: If the permit authorizes demolition or authorizes construction
of a new principal structure, then the applicant shall cause a six foot (6')
chainlink fence to be installed around the perimeter of either the excavation,
the structure under construction or the entire construction area in a location
and manner approved by the building commissioner. The fencing shall be
installed not more than seven (7) days nor less than four (4) days before
commencement of any work on the subject property pursuant to any permit issued
by the village. In addition to such perimeter fencing, the applicant shall
cause safety fencing to be installed around every tree in the parkway abutting
the subject property. Such tree fencing shall be located, so far as feasible,
at the drip line of the tree, whether on public or private property; provided,
however, that this subsection shall not be construed or applied to authorize
placement of tree fencing on private property not owned by the applicant unless
written authorization therefor has been secured from the property owner by the
applicant. If placement of tree fencing is not feasible at the drip line of the
tree, then such fencing shall be installed in a location approved by the
building commissioner. (Ord. 02-03, 5-13-2002)
   F.   Site Preparation Permit Application: Based upon the submissions
required in this section, the building commissioner shall determine whether the
scope of a project for which an applicant seeks a building permit merits the
issuance of a site preparation permit before a building permit may be issued to
minimize damage to the land in question and surrounding property from soil
erosion, damage to stormwater drainage routes, culverts, damage to protected
trees and damage to surrounding streets and to maintain an orderly, secure,
safe and clean construction site. A site preparation permit shall be mandatory
when a tree protection plan is required as part of a tree removal permit. If a
site preparation permit is required, then the applicant shall supply drawings
or narrative responses to address the matters described in this section or to
satisfy applicable provisions of the building code, other ordinances of the
village or other applicable law. Site preparation activities required by a site
preparation may include, without limitation, the following:
      1.   Removal of trees, tree pruning, root pruning, and other tree care
activities that are proposed in the tree removal permit application.
      2.   Installation of protective tree fencing. All protective tree fencing
as required by the Golf tree preservation ordinance (title 4, chapter 6 of this
code).
      3.   Installation of erosion control measures and construction driveway.
      4.   Installation of perimeter area construction fencing as required by
subsection E of this section.
      5.   Installation of temporary markers delineating the limits of
permanent "protected area" markers at the boundaries of wetlands, wetland
buffers, or protected areas proposed to remain undisturbed.
      6.   Shutoff of gas lines or other utilities and disconnection of same
when required.
      7.   Location and delivery of portable toilet and trash receptacle.
      8.   Installation of contractor sign meeting the requirements of section
8-3-7 of this chapter.
      9.   If excavation is required for a new structure, foundation, utility
installation or drainage improvement, the site preparation plan shall indicate
the: a) installation of a single construction entrance, which may be in the
location of the permanent driveway, from the adjoining public or private street
to the lot and b) installation of additional fencing in the construction area
so that all construction traffic to and from the construction area uses the
construction driveway. The construction driveway shall be constructed with
three inch (3") crushed limestone to a minimum compacted depth of six inches
(6"). The site preparation plan shall indicate that, prior to installation of
the construction driveway, the applicant shall be required to install, repair
or replace culverts and ditches so that the natural flow of surface stormwater
on or along the lot is not impeded by the construction driveway or debris and
construction materials. All culverts shall be installed, repaired or replaced
in accordance with village ordinances.
   G.   Issuance Of Site Preparation Permit: If the objectives of minimizing
damage to the land in question and surrounding property and all requirements
relating to site management standards are demonstrated in the site preparation
plan, and if any required street restoration security is posted, and if all
other requirements are satisfied for the issuance of a building permit, then
the building commissioner shall indicate his approval of the site preparation
plan by signing and issuing a site preparation permit to the applicant. Under
the site preparation permit, the applicant shall perform the work indicated in
the site preparation plan and shall not perform any work for which a building
permit must separately be issued unless and until the building permit is
issued. (Ord. 2009-17, 11-9-2009)
8-3-6: SITE MANAGEMENT STANDARDS:
The following site management standards shall apply to all work:
   A.   Accessibility, Parking And Loading Standards: No pavement or sidewalk
within any public right of way shall be unavailable for public use at any time
except when such pavement or sidewalk is removed and replaced. No such pavement
or sidewalk that is removed and replaced shall be out of service for more than
three (3) days without the prior approval of the village. No parking, loading
or storage of demolition debris, spoil or construction materials shall be
permitted within any right of way, on any public property, or within ten feet
(10') of any right of way adjacent public or private property unless
specifically approved by the village. The village may prohibit parking in any
particular location on a public right of way if the village determines that
such parking has an adverse impact on neighboring property or on traffic
control. All uses of vehicles shall comply with applicable codes related to
parking and time of operation of vehicles.
   B.   Particulate Control: Airborne particles shall be controlled at the
subject property at all times during work by means of a water truck and
spraying equipment or other water source capable of spraying and thoroughly
saturating all portions of the structure and surrounding property affected by
the work. Such spraying shall be undertaken at all times necessary to
thoroughly control the creation and migration of airborne particles, including,
without limitation, dust from the subject property.
   C.   Gravel Mat: When determined by the village to be appropriate and
practicable, the applicant shall cause a gravel mat to be installed on the
subject property of a size and in a location sufficient to wash down all
vehicles used on the subject property and to cause dirt and mud to be removed
from the tires of such vehicles. The gravel mat shall be located so as not to
interfere with any use by the public of public rights of way and not to cause
any nuisance or inconvenience to adjacent public or private property.
   D.   Sanitation Facilities: A portable toilet shall be provided at every
site of construction of a new principal structure, or addition thereto, prior
to the commencement of construction, unless an existing facility is available
on the construction site.
   E.   Litter Control And Cleanup: Litter and debris at the subject property
shall be controlled at all times. The applicant shall designate a person
regularly present at the subject property as having responsibility to assure
that no litter or debris leaves the subject property and that all litter and
debris is removed from the subject property before the end of every day,
including weekends regardless of whether or not work was conducted that day on
the subject property.
   F.   Street And Sidewalk Cleaning: The applicant shall cause all dirt, mud,
gravel and other debris from the subject property or related to any work
conducted on the subject property to be cleaned regularly from all sidewalks
and streets adjoining and in the area of the subject property on every day that
construction occurs on said property.
   G.   No Trespass: No permit issued pursuant to the village building code,
shall authorize or shall be construed to authorize any entry onto property
adjoining the subject property or any work for which entry onto property
adjoining the subject property is or may be necessary, unless a proper right of
entry has been secured from the owner of such property.
   H.   Stormwater Management: Stormwater shall be managed during all phases of
demolition and construction so as not to impact adjacent properties and/or
public right of way.
   I.   Wastewater Discharge: No person shall undertake any work pursuant to a
permit issued under the village building code, from which the discharge of any
wastewater will be caused or associated without prior approval. It shall be the
duty of the person undertaking any such work to direct all wastewater flow to
the particular location designated by the building commissioner. No person
undertaking such work shall cause or allow any cement truck wash to be
discharged onto any public property or into any catch basin or other village
sewer facility.
   J.   Limitations On Noise: No person shall operate or cause to be operated
any radio, phonograph, telecommunications device or other such object at such a
volume or in any other manner that would cause a nuisance or a disturbance to
any person. Every contractor and every permittee shall be responsible for all
actions of their employees, agents and subcontractors hereunder, and shall be
liable for all violations of the provisions of this chapter committed by such
employees, agents or subcontractors. (Ord. 02-03, 5-13-2002)
   K.   Permissible Hours And Days Of Construction: All work undertaken
pursuant to a permit issued under the village building code may occur only
between the following hours and on the following days:
7:00 A.M. to 7:00 P.M. on weekdays
8:00 A.M. to 6:00 P.M. on Saturdays
No construction allowed on Sundays or on legal holidays. For purposes of this
subsection, the following are considered legal holidays in the village: New
Year's Day; Memorial Day; Independence Day; Labor Day; Thanksgiving Day; after
twelve o'clock (12:00) noon on Christmas Eve; Christmas Day; and after twelve
o'clock (12:00) noon on New Year's Eve. (Ord. 2015-09, 8-10-2015)
   L.   No Obstructions: No street, parkway or sidewalk shall be obstructed in
the course of any building operations without first securing permission for
such obstruction from the building commissioner. The building commissioner
shall indicate his approval or disapproval of such obstruction upon the permit
issued in connection with the work creating the obstruction.
   M.   Safety Devices: Warnings, barricades and lights shall be maintained
during the course of building operations whenever necessary for the protection
of pedestrians and traffic. The term "building operations" as used in this
section shall apply equally to new construction, remodeling, repairing, moving
and demolition. (Ord. 2009-17, 11-9-2009)
8-3-7: COMMENCEMENT OF DEMOLITION OR CONSTRUCTION:
   A.   Posted Notice: The applicant shall cause notice of demolition or
construction to be given by posting the subject application in a prominent
place with a sign announcing such commencement. Such sign shall include notice
that the rules and regulations applicable to demolition and construction work
are available at the village hall. Such sign shall be posted not less than
fourteen (14) days in advance of such commencement, and shall be maintained on
the subject property until all work on the subject property has been completed
and approved, or until removal of the sign is approved by the building
commissioner or the building inspector.
   B.   Site Restoration: Construction of an approved structure shall have
commenced, or the subject property shall have been fully restored in
conformance with the approved site restoration plan, if any, or with such other
plans as may be approved by the village, within forty five (45) days after
completion of demolition. (Ord. 02-03, 5-13-2002)
8-3-8: PENALTIES:
Any person who violates, disobeys, omits, neglects or refuses to comply with or
resists the enforcement of any of the provisions of this chapter shall be
subject to a class D penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. Each day such violation or failure to comply is permitted
to exist after notification thereof shall constitute a separate offense. No
certificate of occupancy shall be issued for any construction undertaken in
conjunction with the provisions of this chapter until such time that all
penalties and fines have been resolved to the satisfaction of the building
commissioner or the building inspector. (Ord. 2009-17, 11-9-2009)
CHAPTER 4
FIRE PREVENTION REGULATIONS
SECTION:
8-4-1: Bureau Of Fire Prevention
8-4-2: Definitions
8-4-3: Appeals From Decisions Of Fire Prevention Bureau
8-4-4: Modifications
8-4-5: New Materials, Processes Or Occupancies Requiring Permits
8-4-6: Penalties
8-4-7: Code Compliance
8-4-8: Reimbursement For Extraordinary Expenses
8-4-9: Amendments To Life Safety Code
8-4-10: Additional Regulations
8-4-11: Street Obstructions
8-4-12: Excessive False Emergency Alarms
8-4-1: BUREAU OF FIRE PREVENTION:
   A.   Established: The fire prevention code shall be enforced by the bureau
of fire prevention in the fire department of the village of Glenview. The fire
prevention bureau shall be operated under the supervision of the fire marshal
of the fire department. The fire prevention bureau shall be responsible for the
inspection of all properties other than one- and two-family dwellings.
   B.   Inspectors:
      1.   The fire inspector in charge of the bureau of fire prevention shall
be appointed by the fire marshal.
      2.   The fire marshal of the fire department may detail such members of
the fire department as inspectors as shall from time to time be necessary. The
fire marshal of the fire department may recommend to the village board the
employment of technical inspectors who may be members or nonmembers of the fire
department.
   C.   Reports: A report of the bureau of fire prevention shall be made
annually and transmitted to the village clerk. The report shall contain all
proceedings under this code, with such statistics as the fire marshal of the
fire department shall also recommend and any amendments to the code which, in
his judgment, are desirable. (Ord., 6-8-1992)
8-4-2: DEFINITIONS:
As used in the fire prevention code adopted in section
8-1-2 of this title:
CHIEF OF THE FIRE DEPARTMENT OR CHIEF OF THE FIRE PREVENTION BUREAU: The fire
marshal of the village of Glenview.
CORPORATION COUNSEL: The attorney for the village of Golf.
FIREWORKS: As used in the fire prevention code and also held to mean auto
flares.
MUNICIPALITY: The village of Golf. (Ord., 6-8-1992)
8-4-3: APPEALS FROM DECISIONS OF FIRE PREVENTION BUREAU:
Whenever the fire prevention bureau of the fire department shall disapprove an
application or refuse to grant a license or permit applied for, or when it is
claimed that the provisions of the code do not apply or that the true intent
and meaning of the code have been misconstrued or wrongly interpreted, the
applicant may appeal from the decision of the fire prevention bureau to the
fire marshal within thirty (30) days from the date of the decision appealed.
The decision of the fire marshal shall be final.
The fire marshal, when so appealed to, may vary the application of any
provision of this code in any particular case when, in the fire marshal's
judgment, the enforcement would be contrary to the spirit and purpose of this
code or when, in the fire marshal's judgment, the interpretation of the fire
prevention bureau should be modified or reversed. (Ord., 6-8-1992)
8-4-4: MODIFICATIONS:
The fire marshal shall have power to modify any of the provisions of the fire
prevention code upon application, in writing, by the owner or lessee, or his
duly authorized agent, when there are practical difficulties in the way of
carrying out the strict letter of the code, provided that the spirit of the
code shall be observed, public safety secured and substantial justice done. The
particulars of such modification when granted or allowed and the decision of
the fire marshal thereon shall be entered upon the building records of the fire
prevention bureau and a signed copy shall be furnished the applicant. (Ord., 6-
8-1992)
8-4-5: NEW MATERIALS, PROCESSES OR OCCUPANCIES REQUIRING PERMITS:
The building commissioner, the fire marshal of the fire department and the fire
inspector of the bureau of fire prevention shall act as a committee to
determine and specify, after giving affected persons an opportunity to be
heard, any new materials, processes or occupancies, which shall require
permits, in addition to those now enumerated in the code. Following such
determination and specification, the committee shall give written notice
thereof to interested persons. (Ord., 6-8-1992)
8-4-6: PENALTIES:
   A.   Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of the fire
prevention code or fails to comply therewith, or who shall build in violation
of any detailed statement of specifications or plans submitted and approved
thereunder, or any certificate or permit issued thereunder, and from which no
appeal has been taken, or who shall fail to comply with such an order as
affirmed or modified by the fire marshal, or by a court of competent
jurisdiction, within the time fixed herein, shall severally for each and every
such violation and noncompliance respectively, be guilty of a misdemeanor,
punishable by a fine as provided in the general penalty in section
1-4-2 of this code. The imposition of one penalty for any violation shall not
excuse the violation or permit it to continue; and all such persons shall be
required to correct or remedy such violations or defects within the time
reasonably necessary as determined and specified, in writing, by the fire
marshal, or within such further time as may be extended by him in writing; and
when not otherwise specified, each ten (10) days that prohibited conditions are
maintained shall constitute a separate offense. (Ord., 6-8-1992; amd. 2003
Code)
   B.   The application of the above penalty shall not be held to prevent the
enforced removal of prohibited conditions. (Ord., 6-8-1992)
8-4-7: CODE COMPLIANCE:
Whenever a physical change is made to a structure for which a building or
remodeling permit is required, or a change of the type of occupancy occurs
which, in the opinion of the fire marshal, creates a greater hazard to public
safety or welfare, said property shall be brought into compliance with all
codes adopted by the village relative to the protection of health, safety and
welfare. (Ord., 6-8-1992)
8-4-8: REIMBURSEMENT FOR EXTRAORDINARY EXPENSES:
   A.   Upon report and recommendation of the fire department, the corporate
authorities find and determine that the recipients of aid or emergency relief
and services shall be assessed for extraordinary costs incurred and payable to
third parties or village personnel for costs associated with rendering aid or
emergency relief and services, including provision of supplies and equipment
exhausted in rendering of said aid or emergency relief and services; and
   B.   Examples of such items to be billed to persons receiving aid or
emergency relief and services include, but are not limited to, services by
third parties relative to plumbing work within property lot lines, removal of
vehicles or other items necessitating use of special equipment, testing to
determine life safety factors when required, handling or disposing of toxic or
hazardous substances and other related or necessary emergency relief and
services; and
      1.   That the recipients or benefactors or administrators, personal
representatives, executors, successors, heirs or assigns thereof, all as
determined by the head of the department rendering aid or emergency relief,
shall be and are obligated to reimburse the village in the actual amount of
payment made by the village to third parties for services rendered in providing
aid or emergency relief and for personnel costs associated with this aid, as
well as payments to replenish necessary supplies and equipment used while
providing aid or emergency services. The village of Glenview, upon incurring
such extraordinary costs, shall notify the Golf village clerk of the
circumstances and provide a copy of the invoice or billing statement from the
third party that specifies the nature of the expenditures and the amount to be
or, in fact, paid. The Golf village clerk shall cause an invoice to be issued
for the amount certified by the village of Glenview as to each circumstance
reported.
      2.   As used herein, the term "third party" means and includes any
person, company or business entity, other than the village or its employees.
The village may not employ any person or entity as a third party directly or
indirectly sharing an interest in such services with an employee or officer of
the village, nor a company of which any portion is owned by an employee or
officer of the village.
      3.   The village shall allow for a reasonable time for the payment of the
reimbursement amount and shall hear any complaints or objections on the type
and amounts of the expense. The village of Glenview or Golf may adjust the
amounts invoiced based upon demonstrated hardship but is not required to so
adjust. In the event that no payment or response to request for reimbursement
has been received within thirty (30) days from the date of invoice, the village
is authorized to undertake such action as provided by law for the recovery of
money due the village, including, but not limited to, the filing of a lien in
the office of the recorder of deeds or the office of the registrar or titles of
Cook County. (Ord., 6-8-1992)
8-4-9: AMENDMENTS TO LIFE SAFETY CODE:
The 1985 edition of the life safety code, as adopted in section
8-1-2 of this title, is amended as follows:
Section 5-4.1.1. Add the following to the end of the subsection:
Exception No. 1: All occupancy classifications except for residential shall
have a minimum of two (2) exits remote as possible from each other.
Section 5-8. Add a new subsection 5-8.1.6 to read as follows:
Battery operated emergency lighting shall be provided, where required by the
Glenview fire prevention bureau, in all occupancies other than one- and two-
family dwellings.
   (Ord., 6-8-1992)
8-4-10: ADDITIONAL REGULATIONS:
   A.   Liquefied Petroleum Gases:
      1.   The bulk storage of liquefied petroleum gases within the boundaries
of the village as established from time to time in the zoning ordinance of the
village 1 , is strictly prohibited.
      2.   Portable tank storage shall be allowed as follows providing all NFPA
requirements are met:
         a.   Commercial: A total of twelve (12) 20-pound cylinders.
         b.   Construction: Portable cylinders used for heating purposes shall
be allowed in an amount acceptable to the fire prevention bureau.
The filling of cylinders within the boundaries of the village is strictly
prohibited.
   B.   Flammable And Combustible Liquids: Flammable and combustible liquids
aboveground tank storage is prohibited in any and all use districts within the
boundaries of the village as established from time to time in the zoning
ordinance of the village.
   C.   Explosives And Blasting Agents: The manufacture, possession, storage,
sale, transportation or use of explosives or blasting agents within the
boundaries of the village is prohibited. (Ord., 6-8-1992)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 9 of this code.
8-4-11: STREET OBSTRUCTIONS:
No person shall erect, construct, place or maintain any bumps, fences, gates,
chains, bars, pipes, wood or metal horses or any other type of obstruction in
or on any street within the boundaries of the village without the express
written permission of the village board. The village board shall, prior to
issuing such approval, obtain an opinion from the chief of the Glenview fire
department regarding the impact any obstruction might have on public safety.
The word "street", as used in this section, shall mean any roadway, accessible
to the public for vehicular traffic, including, but not limited to, private
streets or access lanes, as well as all public streets and highways within the
boundaries of the village. (Ord., 6-8-1992)
8-4-12: EXCESSIVE FALSE EMERGENCY ALARMS:
   A.   Definitions: For purposes of this section:
    ALARM SYSTEM: Any assemblage of mechanical or electrical equipment or
devices or a single device, such as a solid state unit which plugs directly
into a one hundred ten (110) volt AC line, arranged to signal the presence of a
hazard, occurrence of an unauthorized intrusion or other activity requiring
urgent and immediate attention. The term alarm system shall include the terms
"automatic holdup alarm system", "holdup alarm system", "burglar alarm system",
"fire alarm system", "smoke detection alarm system", and "carbon monoxide alarm
system". The alarm system can be a receiving station alarm, having a direct
burglar, fire or smoke alarm connection from any building, place or premises
within the village of Golf at the village of Golf, Cook County or any other
police department or the village of Glenview or any other fire department, an
independent alarm system that emits an audible sound to the exterior of the
premises, or a central station alarm system which relays the signal to a
private person or company, either within or without the boundaries of the
village of Golf, providing watchmen or security service, or providing a service
to contact the village of Golf or any other police department, the village of
Glenview or any other fire department or any other emergency personnel of the
village of Golf or any other village. Personal medical alert alarm systems are
not included in this section.
   FALSE ALARM: Any alarm signal (burglar, fire, smoke, carbon monoxide, or
otherwise) eliciting a response by village of Golf police personnel or any
other village's police personnel, the village of Glenview or any other fire
emergency personnel, or any other emergency personnel wherein an emergency
situation does not, in fact, exist but does not include an alarm caused by
violent conditions of nature (severe weather), power outages, or other
extraordinary circumstances not reasonably subject to control by the property
owner/alarm user.
   B.   Charges: The property owner of any residence or commercial
establishment at which more than two (2) false alarms occur within a calendar
year shall be subject to the charges set forth in the annual fee schedule as
adopted by the village board. For the year in which the ordinance codified
herein is adopted (i.e., the calendar year 2009), such charges shall be as set
forth in the following chart:
 
3 through 6 false alarms $120.00 per false alarm
Over 6 false alarms      200.00 per false alarm
 
The charges which any property owner has been assessed pursuant to this section
(in the amount set forth above or as amended in any year's annual fee schedule)
shall be paid to the village of Golf within thirty (30) days from the invoice
date requesting such charges. All unpaid false alarm charges will be referred
to an authorized collection agency.
   C.   Officer In Charge; Responsibilities To Document False Alarms: The
officer in charge of an incident which resulted from the activation of an
"alarm system" as defined in this section shall include in his report made as a
result of such incident, information regarding the type of alarm (i.e.,
intrusion/holdup/fire station alarm/central station alarm or outside ringer)
and shall also indicate whether or not any evidence exists of actual intrusion
or fire or other public safety concern which would have activated the alarm
system. The officer in charge shall also comment as to whether the alarm
activation was by act of God or other means which may be proven to be the cause
of the alarm activation and which may indicate that activation of the alarm was
clearly beyond the property owner/alarm user's responsibility or control.
   D.   Notice Of False Alarms: The chief of police of the village of Golf or
his designated agent shall notify the property owner/alarm user after the
village of Golf police department recorded two (2) false alarms within a
calendar year. The village of Golf police department shall notify the property
owner/alarm user in writing by first class mail of such fact and that
additional false alarm occurrences will result in the imposition of service
charges in accordance with this section. Upon additional false alarm
occurrences, the village of Golf shall invoice the property owner/alarm user as
specified in this section. Each property owner/alarm user shall have the
opportunity within ten (10) days after the receipt of such notice to submit a
report to or meet with the village of Golf chief of police or his designated
agent for the purpose of showing cause as to whether circumstances exist so as
to warrant a voiding of any prior false alarm recordation. The decision of the
village of Golf chief of police or his designated agent as to whether a false
alarm occurred shall be final.
   E.   Grace Periods For False Alarms: Whenever a new alarm system is
installed or a new property owner/alarm user (new resident or business) takes
control of an existing alarm system, the property owner/alarm user shall be
given sixty (60) days from the date of the installation or occupancy within
which no alarm from the premises shall be deemed to be a false alarm. (Ord.
2009-15, 10-19-2009)
CHAPTER 5
FENCES
SECTION:
8-5-1: Purpose
8-5-2: Definitions
8-5-3: Fence Permit
8-5-4: Fence Restrictions; Exceptions
8-5-5: Notice Of Violations; Failure To Comply
8-5-6: Height Modifications For Golf Road
8-5-7: Penalties
8-5-1: PURPOSE:
This chapter, which is known as the FENCE ORDINANCE, is enacted in accordance
with and in furtherance of the Village plan 1  to maintain the aesthetics and
spacious atmosphere of an entirely single-family, residential and semirural
community. (Ord., 3-13-1967)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 10, chapter 1 of this Code.
8-5-2: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, certain terms are to be defined as follows:
BUILDING LINE: A line parallel with a lot line and extended from the actual
closest wall of any existing building to any such lot line.
FENCE: Any freestanding structure or barrier of metal, masonry, composition,
wood or of whatsoever material as may exist as a boundary or a means of
protection, confinement or screening, which rests on or is partially buried
into the ground and rises above ground level.
FRONT YARD: A yard or unoccupied space on the same lot with any building or
structure extending along the entire length of the front lot line back to a
line drawn parallel with said front lot line at a distance equal to the depth
of the permissible building setback or the actual building line of any existing
building.
HISTORIC FENCE: A post and board wood fence consisting generally of three (3)
evenly spaced, horizontal boards that are installed on vertical posts set
approximately eight feet (8') apart, with all boards and posts painted white
and with the posts not exceeding the maximum height of any adjacent historic
fence.
LOT: Land occupied or to be occupied by one building and accessory buildings
and uses and including the open spaces required under the zoning regulations of
this Code. A lot may be land so recorded on the records of Cook County,
Illinois, or may be a part of or a combination of lots so recorded.
PROHIBITED FENCE: Any fence that consists of or includes snow fencing, chicken
wire fencing, hog wire fencing, electrified fences, spiked fences, barbed wire,
and other non-customary residential materials, provided that chicken wire up to
18 inches in height from the base of a wood fence may be used to protect
against burrowing animals and in such application is not a prohibited fence.
REAR YARD: An open space (unoccupied except for accessory buildings) on the
same lot with a building between the rear line of a building and the rear line
of the lot for the full width of the lot except as modified by side yard
restrictions.
SETBACK: The minimum horizontal distance between the street wall or walls of
the building and the street line.
SIDE YARD: An open unoccupied space on the same lot with a building between the
main wall of the building and the side line of the lot and extending from the
front lot line to the rear yard.
YARD: Any space or grounds abutting, surrounding or surrounded by any building
or buildings.
(Ord., 3-13-1967; amd. 1989 Code; 2003 Code; Ord. 2017-04, 6-12-2017; Ord.
2021-02, 6-14-2021)
8-5-3: FENCE PERMIT:
No fence whatever shall be erected within the Village without application to
the Building Commissioner for a permit and any such application shall be on
forms provided by the Building Commissioner and shall be accompanied by a
permit fee as provided in section 8-1-5 of this title, and a survey of the
property to be fenced. If the permit is not denied by the Building Commissioner
within ten (10) days after application in accord herewith, it shall be deemed
to have been issued. Notwithstanding the foregoing provisions, a prohibited
fence is not allowed in the village and a fence permit shall not be issued for
any prohibited fence.
(Ord., 3-13-1967; Ord. 2021-02, 6-14-2021)
8-5-4: FENCE RESTRICTIONS; EXCEPTIONS:
   A.   No fence of any kind or size shall be permitted or shall hereafter be
erected in any front yard, as defined in this chapter, with certain exceptions
noted in subsection F of this section.
   B.   No fence shall be permitted within the side yard or rear yard in excess
of six feet (6') in height. Any fence that the building commissioner approved
with a height of six feet (6') under previous fence regulations shall be deemed
approved as a matter of right under this section.
   C.   No fence shall be erected on lot lines, except that fences may be
located at the lot line of any lot which constitutes a Village boundary or
faces immediately upon Golf Road or the Soo Line Railroad tracks or on more
than one lot.
   D.   No fence shall be constructed on a lot alongside a street or alley or
within five feet (5') of such street or alley and parallel thereto of greater
height than five feet (5') above the surface of the street or alley where a
grade is established or five feet (5') above the surface of the street or alley
where no grade is established; provided, however, in the case of a fence
located in a rear yard abutting Overlook Drive or located in any yard abutting
Golf Road, the METRA right-of-way or Diederick Park, a fence up to six (6) feet
in height may be constructed.
   E.   No single or isolated wall of any material whatever, which forms no
part of a building or structure lawfully erected, shall be constructed upon any
portion of a lot where the distance from such wall to the lot line is less than
the height of the wall and unless such isolated wall shall have lateral
supports on at least one side of same with braces extending to the top of the
wall and is so constructed that it shall be capable of resisting a horizontal
wind pressure on every part of same twice as great as buildings under the
provisions of this title must be designed to resist.
   F.   The prohibitions herein shall not apply to the following:
      1.   Any fences existing or to be erected on land that is zoned PCC
Property District; but nothing herein shall be construed to vary or lessen the
fencing requirements of the Village swimming pool ordinance.
      2.   Historic fences may be installed in front yards bordering the right-
of-way of Overlook Drive, between the entrance to the Village at Golf Road and
the intersection of Briar Road and Overlook Drive, provided that such fences
continue along the entire front lot line and align with the historic fences
already existing on Overlook Drive so as to appear as a continuation of
existing historic fences. Historic fences as so authorized may be extended
across all front yards of a lot even if certain front yards of such lot are not
located on Overlook Drive. (Ord. 2017-04, 6-12-2017)
      3.   For the purpose of aligning historic fences on Overlook Drive, the
owner of a lot may lawfully apply for and receive a conditional permit for a
historic fence to occupy part of the right-of-way of Overlook Drive
("conditional ROW permit"). The application for a conditional ROW permit shall
be on such forms and shall include such items as the Village may require,
including drawings, dimensions, elevations, details, north arrow, street names,
a copy of a valid deed to the owner and payment of the appropriate permit fee
as set forth in the Village fee schedule. The Village (by the Building
Commissioner or other designee) in its sole discretion will determine criteria
for placement of historic fences in the right-of-way ("placement criteria")
based on potential conflicts with the Americans With Disabilities Act, the
Illinois Accessibility Code, public utilities, parkway trees, pedestrian and
vehicular traffic and public safety. Notwithstanding the general terms of any
conditional ROW permit, if any portion of the historic fence (such as a
moveable gate) restricts vehicular passage from the adjoining street, such gate
shall be situated to allow for at least twenty feet (20') of driveway extending
between such gate and the street in which automobiles can wait while the gate
is operated. Approval of any moveable gate shall be at the discretion of the
Village Board. If approved, any moveable gate shall be subject to such terms
and conditions as the Village Board may impose for the purpose of assuring
emergency access. A conditional ROW permit will not expire, provided the terms
and conditions thereof continue to be met. The use and occupancy of the Village
right-of-way by any historic fence (whether or not a conditional ROW permit is
then in effect) shall at all times be subject to the following terms and
conditions:
         a.   The historic fence shall comply with the applicable provisions of
this chapter. Specific safety requirements listed as conditions of an
applicable conditional ROW permit must be observed.
         b.   Each owner with a historic fence located in Village right-of- way
shall provide updated owner contact information to the Village upon request.
         c.   Upon thirty (30) days' prior notice to the owner (except if an
emergency arises and such advance notice cannot be given without imperiling
public safety, in which event the Village shall give such notice before or
after taking action as may then be feasible): 1) the Village may revoke a
conditional ROW permit in whole or in part, if necessary to observe more
stringent placement criteria that, in the sole judgment of the Village Board,
should be observed to comply with law or better promote the public health,
safety and general welfare of the residents of the Village or 2) the Village
may require the owner to remove or relocate all or part of such owner's
historic fence in the event of any conflict with road repairs or utility work
that will take place in the right-of-way. The owner of a historic fence shall
bear all costs of removal, relocation and replacement of such owner's historic
fence without contribution from the Village.
         d.   Each owner of a lot having a historic fence located in Village
right-of-way shall indemnify, defend and hold harmless the Village, its agents,
servants, and employees and each of them against and hold it and them harmless
from any and all lawsuits, claims, demands, liabilities, losses and expenses,
including court costs and attorney's fees, for or on account of any injury to
any person, or any death at any time resulting from such injury, or any damage
to property, which may arise or which may be alleged to have arisen out of or
in connection with the issuance of the conditional ROW permit or with the
placement, maintenance or repair of such historic fence in the right-of-way of
the Village. The foregoing indemnity shall apply except if such injury, death
or damage is caused directly by the willful and wanton conduct of the Village,
its agents, servants, or employees or any other person indemnified hereunder.
         e.   If the owner of a lot having a historic fence located in Village
right-of-way shall fail or refuse to remove or relocate the fence when required
by the Village, the person violating these provisions shall be subject to a
Class C penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code, and the Village shall have the right to enforce such
removal by equitable proceedings and, without liability to the owner, the
Village shall also have the right to remove the fence through its own
contractors. In such event, the Village shall be entitled to recover from such
owner the costs of such removal. The Village may establish the amounts so due
through administrative adjudication or by civil action, and if any such amounts
are not paid to the Village upon demand, the Village Clerk, or designated
representative, is authorized, in accordance with law, to file a notice of lien
in the Office of Recorder of Deeds of Cook County, to foreclose the lien, and
to sue the occupant or owner of the lot to recover the charges and penalty due,
plus attorney fees as established by the court, including the costs of filing
the notice of lien, foreclosing the lien, and all litigation costs incurred in
connection with the collection of the amount due.
(Ord. 2017-04, 6-12-2017; amd. Ord. 2018-01, 1-8-2018; Ord. 2021-02, 6-14-2021)
8-5-5: NOTICE OF VIOLATIONS; FAILURE TO COMPLY:
In all cases where a fence or wall shall hereafter be erected contrary to the
provisions of this chapter, the Building Commissioner shall forthwith notify
the owner or agent of the land on which same is located, or the contractor
engaged in erecting same, and shall briefly specify in such notice in what
manner such fence or wall violates the provisions of this chapter, and the
Building Commissioner shall require the person so notified to forthwith make
such fence or wall conform to and comply with the provisions of this chapter,
specifying in such notice the time within which such work shall be done.
If, at the expiration of the time set in the notice provided for in this
section, the person so notified shall have refused, neglected or failed to
comply with the request made in such notice and shall not have torn down or
changed the said fence or wall so as to conform to and comply with the
provisions of this chapter, the Building Commissioner shall have authority and
it shall be his duty to proceed forthwith to tear down, or cause to be torn
down, such fence or wall or so much thereof as is being maintained or shall
have been erected and constructed in violation of the provisions hereof, and
the cost of such tearing down shall be charged to and recovered from the owner
of such fence or wall or from the person for whom such fence or wall has been
or is being erected. (Ord., 11-13-1928; amd. 1989 Code)
8-5-6: HEIGHT MODIFICATIONS FOR GOLF ROAD:
Notwithstanding the height limits established in subsections
8-5-4:D of this chapter, in the case of a proposed fence located in any yard
abutting Golf Road, which fence is replacing an existing fence, (i) the
replacement fence may match the height of the existing fence but not to exceed
seven (7) feet in height and (ii) the Zoning Board of Appeals may authorize the
same height for an interior side yard fence connecting to the fence abutting
Golf Road. The Zoning Board of Appeals shall not authorize any fence height
modifications under this section unless it finds that the fence at the
increased height will not impair the integrity and character of the
neighborhood in which the fence is located or be detrimental or injurious to
the other property or improvements in the general vicinity in which the
property is located.
(Ord. 2021-02, 6-14-2021)
8-5-7: PENALTIES:
Any person who shall erect, construct or maintain a fence in violation hereof
or who shall otherwise refuse to comply herewith shall be subject to a Class A
penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. (Ord., 3-13-1967; amd. 1989 Code)
Each and every violation, and each and every day or part thereof such violation
or failure to comply continues following three (3) days after notification
thereof is sent by registered mail, shall constitute a separate offense. (Ord.
9410, 12-12-1994)
CHAPTER 6
PRIVATE RESIDENTIAL SWIMMING POOLS
SECTION:
8-6-1: Title
8-6-2: Definitions
8-6-3: Compliance With Building And Zoning Regulations
8-6-4: Permit Required; Fee
8-6-5: Design And Construction
8-6-6: Fences
8-6-7: Operation And Maintenance
8-6-7-1: Required Equipment
8-6-7-2: Water Supply
8-6-7-3: Water Condition
8-6-7-4: Drainage Of Pool Water
8-6-7-5: Sanitary Premises And Facilities
8-6-8: Noisy Conditions Prohibited
8-6-9: Inspections
8-6-10: Exemptions From Provisions
8-6-11: Penalties
8-6-1: TITLE:
This chapter shall be known and may be cited as the PRIVATE RESIDENTIAL
SWIMMING POOL ORDINANCE OF THE VILLAGE OF GOLF. (Ord., 10-1966)
8-6-2: DEFINITIONS:
PRIVATE RESIDENTIAL SWIMMING POOL: Any swimming or wading pool over two feet
(2') in depth, or with a surface area exceeding two hundred fifty (250) square
feet. This shall include portable or temporary type pools, hot tubs and spas
installed entirely above ground; except that installation permits and drawings
and plans shall not apply to such pools. (Ord., 10-1966; amd. 2003 Code)
8-6-3: COMPLIANCE WITH BUILDING AND ZONING REGULATIONS:
