9-7-7: PENALTIES:
Any person who violates, disobeys, omits, neglects or refuses to comply with,
or who resists the enforcement of any of the provisions of this title shall,
upon conviction, be subject to a Class B penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. (Ord., 4-22-1943; amd. 1989 Code; Ord. 03-05, 9-8-2003)
Each and every violation, and each and every day or part thereof such violation
or failure to comply continues following three (3) days after notification
thereof is sent by registered mail, shall constitute a separate offense. (Ord.
9410, 12-12-1994; amd. Ord. 03-05, 9-8-2003)
TITLE 10
SUBDIVISIONS
CHAPTER 1
OFFICIAL VILLAGE PLAN
SECTION:
10-1-1: Short Title
10-1-2: Adoption Of Plan
10-1-3: Purpose And Contents Of Plan
10-1-1: SHORT TITLE:
This chapter shall be known as the OFFICIAL VILLAGE PLAN for the village.
(Ord., 6-13-1949; amd. 1989 Code)
10-1-2: ADOPTION OF PLAN:
The comprehensive plan of public improvements looking to the present and future
development of the village and regulating land subdivisions within the
corporate limits, which plan has been prepared and recommended to the village
board of trustees by the building commissioner is hereby adopted and made the
official village plan. (Ord., 6-13-1949; amd. 1989 Code)
10-1-3: PURPOSE AND CONTENTS OF PLAN:
The plan as hereby adopted consists of the following:
   A.   Objectives:
      1.   That the character of the village and its environs as a strictly
residential community of individual homes be maintained; and
      2.   That for the promotion of the public health, safety and convenience,
and for the attainment of maximum and practical utility, beauty and
attractiveness and for the maintenance and protection of property values, all
future developments in the village shall provide:
         a.   That an adequate circulatory water supply system be completed and
maintained;
         b.   That an adequate system of sanitary and drainage sewers be
installed and maintained;
         c.   That streets be of adequate width and without jogs, sharp turns
and dangerous intersections;
         d.   That the planting of desirable and long lived trees be uniform
throughout the village; and (Ord., 6-13-1949)
         e.   That the architectural design and location of public buildings be
approved by the building commissioner before construction is commenced. (Ord.,
6-13-1949; amd. 1989 Code)
   B.   Map: Map no. 2 entitled official plan map of the village of Golf, Cook
County, Illinois; and (Ord. 68-4, 7-31-1968)
   C.   Regulations: The subdivision regulations set forth in this title.
(Ord., 6-13-1949)
CHAPTER 2
SUBDIVISION REGULATIONS
SECTION:
10-2-1: Short Title
10-2-2: Definitions
10-2-3: Conformance With Village Plan
10-2-4: Plats And Procedures
10-2-4-1: Tentative Plat
10-2-4-2: Final Plat
10-2-5: Required Improvements
10-2-6: Variations
10-2-7: Interpretation
10-2-8: Enforcement
10-2-9: Penalty
10-2-1: SHORT TITLE:
This chapter shall be known as the SUBDIVISION REGULATIONS for the village.
(Ord., 6-13-1949; amd. 1989 Code)
10-2-2: DEFINITIONS:
LAND SUBDIVISION: Any change, resubdivision or rearrangement in the boundary or
division lines of a parcel of property or public thoroughfare. (Ord., 6-13-
1949)
10-2-3: CONFORMANCE WITH VILLAGE PLAN:
After the effective date hereof, no map or plat of any subdivision presented
for record affecting land within the corporate limits of the village or in
contiguous territory outside of and distant not more than one and one-half (11/
2) miles from such limits and not included in any city, village or incorporated
town shall be entitled to record or shall be valid unless the subdivision
thereon shown shall provide for streets, alleys and public grounds in
conformity with the requirement of the plan applicable thereto 1 . (Ord., 6-13-
1949)
 
Notes
1 1. 65 ILCS 5/11-12-6.
10-2-4: PLATS AND PROCEDURES:
10-2-4-1: TENTATIVE PLAT:
   A.   Submission: Any owner of land within the corporate limits of the
village or contiguous unincorporated territory one and one-half (11/2) miles
beyond such corporate limits wishing to divide the same into building lots for
the purpose of sale and assessment or both, and wishing to dedicate streets and
alleys and other lands for public use, shall first submit to the village board
a tentative plat in duplicate blueprints.
   B.   Requirements: The tentative plat shall meet the following requirements:
      1.   Scale: Each tentative plat shall be drawn to the scale of one
hundred feet to one inch (100' = 1").
      2.   Boundaries: The tentative plat shall show the boundaries of the
property to be subdivided, section and half section lines, existing permanent
buildings, watercourses and other existing features pertinent to proper
subdivision, together with building restrictions to be imposed on the property.
      3.   Municipal Boundaries: All corporate boundary lines within or
adjacent to the proposed subdivision shall be shown and designated.
      4.   Contours: Contour lines at intervals of not more than two feet (2')
shall be shown when required by the building commissioner. (Ord., 6-13-1949;
amd. 1989 Code)
      5.   Streets: The widths of streets (with their names) and alleys,
dimensions of lots and blocks and building lines shall be shown. The surveyed
locations and full widths of streets (with their names) bounding the proposed
subdivision and the widths and names of intersecting streets in the property
immediately adjacent shall be shown. All streets shall be carried to the
boundaries of the proposed subdivision.
      6.   Names: The name of the proposed subdivision with the name of the
owner, sponsor or trustees shall be shown. (Ord., 6-13-1949)
   C.   Action By Village Authorities:
      1.   The village board shall by motion refer the tentative plat to the
building commissioner and shall at the same time instruct the village engineer
to collaborate with the subdivider and the building commissioner for the
purpose of preparing estimates of cost of street grading and such other public
improvements as are contemplated by the subdivider and shown on his tentative
plat. Such public improvements contemplated and shown shall comply with the
provisions of this chapter.
      2.   The building commissioner shall then approve or disapprove the
tentative plat; provided, however, that if the tentative plat is not
satisfactory as originally presented, the building commissioner may cause the
subdivider to make such changes as may be required by the building commissioner
and thereupon approve the same. Upon approval of the tentative plat, the
following statement signed by the building commissioner shall be stamped upon
both copies thereof:
   NOTICE OF APPROVAL
Notice is hereby given that the general plan of the subdivision shown in this
tentative plat has received approval of the building commissioner of the
village of Golf and that the said building commissioner is now ready to receive
the final plat for consideration.
      Date                      The building commissioner of
         the village of Golf, Illinois.
                                             
One copy of the approved plat shall thereupon be returned to the subdivider,
the other copy shall be retained by the building commissioner. (Ord., 6-13-
1949)
10-2-4-2: FINAL PLAT:
   A.   Submission; Supporting Documents: After the building commissioner has
approved the tentative plat, the subdivider shall submit to the building
commissioner a final plat, surveyed by a registered Illinois land surveyor, and
prepared for record in accordance with the provisions of subsection B of this
section, together with the following supporting documents:
      1.   A grading and paving plan and profiles approved by the village
engineer showing the center line elevations of all existing streets and alleys
in the proposed subdivision and the center line elevations of all proposed
street and alley pavement. Elevations shall be referred to some permanent bench
mark. Profiles shall be drawn to a horizontal scale of fifty feet to one inch
(50' = 1") and vertical scale of five feet to one inch (5' = 1").
      2.   A statement signed by the subdivider setting forth the public
improvements he proposes to make in the subdivision, together with plans and
specifications, clearly describing the same and agreeing to make the said
improvements at his own expense, subject to approval of the final plat by the
village board within the time limit fixed by the building commissioner.
      3.   A statement of approval signed by the village engineer certifying
that the improvements described in the subdivider's statement meet the minimum
requirements of this title, and giving an estimate of the cost of such
improvements, including the cost of engineering and inspection.
      4.   A duly executed corporate completion bond, posted with the village
by the subdivider, in an amount equal to the village engineer's estimate,
securing the satisfactory completion of all public improvements in strict
accordance with the description, plans and specifications submitted by the
subdivider and approved by the building commissioner.
      5.   Evidence satisfactory to the building commissioner showing title in
the subdivider and that all taxes and special assessments due on the property
to be subdivided have been paid.
   B.   Contents Of Final Plat; Design Requirements: The final plat to be
submitted to the building commissioner shall be in strict accordance with the
approved tentative plat and shall be drawn on tracing cloth to a scale of not
less than one hundred feet to one inch (100' = 1"). One blueprint of the said
final plat shall accompany the same. The final plat shall meet the following
requirements:
      1.   Name: The name of the proposed subdivision shall be shown.
      2.   Date: The date of preparation and a proper north sign shall be
shown.
      3.   Survey: A correct survey of the property proposed to be platted
shall be shown.
      4.   Legal Description: A legal description of the property shall be
given which includes reference to the section, township and range, government
section lines and corners, half section lines, the location and dimension of
all streets (with their names), alleys and all other lands to be dedicated to
public use; and the lines and dimension of abutting roads and streets (with
their names) and alleys shall be shown.
      5.   Lot Lines: All lot lines shall be shown, lots and blocks numbered or
lettered; building lines and easements shall be shown and determined by
measurements.
      6.   Dimensions: All necessary dimensions both linear and angular shall
be shown. Linear dimensions shall be shown in feet and decimals of a foot, and
all deflection angles, all radii, arcs and central angles of all corners along
the property line of each street shall be shown.
      7.   Monuments: The description and location of all survey monuments
erected in the subdivision shall be shown. Such monuments shall be either iron
pipe not less than three-quarters inch (3/4") in diameter and thirty inches
(30") long, or stone or concrete not less than four inches (4") in diameter and
twenty four inches (24") long. Monuments shall be erected at all street and lot
corners, at all points where street lines intersect the exterior boundaries of
the subdivision and at angle points and points of curve in each street.
      8.   Street Connections: Provisions shall be made for direct connections
with the existing streets in adjoining subdivisions.
      9.   Dedication Of Lands For Public Use: The plat shall have lettered
upon it a statement of dedication properly conveying all lands dedicated for
such public uses as streets, public schools, parks or any other public use, and
there shall be attached to the plat a certificate of title certifying the
ownership of all such lands to be so dedicated by the said plat. Public grounds
other than streets, alleys and parking areas shall be dedicated in appropriate
locations by the plat at the rate of at least one acre for each sixty (60)
residential building sites or family living units, which may be accommodated
under the zoning or other restrictions applying to the land.
      10.   Building Restrictions: Detail of building restrictions to be
imposed on the property by the subdivider shall be shown.
      11.   Certificates, Etc.: All proper certificates, seals and signatures
as required by law shall be shown.
      12.   Easements: Where no alleys are platted, easements not less than
eight feet (8') wide shall be provided across the rear of all lots for any or
all public utilities, including communication lines, electric lines, and other
similar utilities or entities which have received a franchise or permit from
the Village in the subdivision or in the rights-of-way adjacent to the
subdivision. All such utilities shall be placed underground in protected
easements and the easements shall be so laid out that a proper continuity may
be had for such utilities from block to block and in a manner that will not
conflict with other underground services. Underground utilities shall be
located in conduit as required by the utility. All transformer boxes shall be
located so as not be unsightly or hazardous to the public. No public utility
easements shall be located in the front yards or side yards of any lots.
   C.   Approval Of Final Plat:
      1.   Building Commissioner Approval: When the building commissioner has
approved the final plat, the following official stamp shall be stamped or
lettered upon the said final plat, signed by the building commissioner and
attested by his secretary:
Approved by the building commissioner of Golf, Cook County, Illinois, this
        day of                    , 19     .
         Signed                                           
The building commissioner shall then transmit the approved final plat to the
village board, together with a letter of transmittal calling attention to all
variations, if any, approved by the building commissioner and setting forth its
reasons for approving the same, and conveying such other information concerning
the final plat as the building commissioner may deem necessary.
With the approved final plat, the building commissioner shall also transmit to
the village board the subdivider's agreement with respect to improvements and
all plans, specifications, estimates, completion bonds and all other documents,
certificates and papers pertaining to the final plat and the subdivision
platted thereon. (Ord., 6-13-1949; amd. 1989 Code)
      2.   Final Approval By Village Board Of Trustees: When the village board
is satisfied with the final plat and with all improvements, conditions and
documents pertaining to the subdivision platted thereon, the village board
shall by resolution approve the said plat and authorize and direct the village
president to approve and sign the plat for and in the name of the village. Said
approval shall be sealed with the corporate seal of the village and attested by
the village clerk.
(Ord., 6-13-1949; amd. 1989 Code; 2003 Code; Ord. 2020-03, 5-11-2020)
10-2-5: REQUIRED IMPROVEMENTS:
   A.   Roadway Improvements: The subdivider shall at his own expense improve
all streets with a roadway not less than twenty five feet (25') wide (back to
back of curbs) consisting of approved macadam or concrete pavement not less
than eight inches (8") thick.
   B.   Additional Improvements: The subdivider of any proposed subdivision
lying within the village limits shall also provide at his own expense public
improvements as follows: (Ord., 6-13-1949)
      1.   Street Trees: Street trees shall be planted throughout the entire
subdivision. Such trees shall be planted in the parkways, shall be not less
than fifty feet (50') apart and shall be desirable long lived trees. (Ord., 6-
13-1949; amd. 1989 Code; 2003 Code)
      2.   Street Name Signs: Street name signs of a type approved by the
village board shall be provided at all street intersections.
      3.   Water Mains: The water system of the village shall be extended
throughout the entire subdivision in such a manner that every lot in such
subdivision may be serviced by means of a house connection within its own
frontage 1 .
      4.   Fire Hydrants 2 : Fire hydrants shall be installed throughout the
entire subdivision at intervals not exceeding four hundred feet (400'). No fire
hydrant shall be connected to any water main which is less than six inches (6")
in diameter. All fire hydrants shall conform with village specifications 3 .
      5.   Sanitary Sewers: A complete system of sanitary sewers shall be
constructed throughout the entire subdivision in such a manner as to render the
same accessible to every lot within its own frontage.
      6.   Storm Sewers: A storm sewer system shall be constructed throughout
the entire subdivision which shall be separate and independent of the sanitary
sewer system, in accordance with requirements of the village board. (Ord., 6-
13-1949)
   C.   Approval Of Plans And Specifications: All plans and specifications and
contracts for public improvements required by this chapter such as street
paving, sidewalks, water system and sewer systems shall be approved by the
village board before starting construction.
   D.   Building Permit Requirements: No construction of such public
improvements shall commence unless a building permit authorizing such
construction shall first have been applied for and procured from the building
commissioner. The building commissioner shall issue such permit only after the
approval of the final plat by the village board of trustees provided for in
this section, and after the payment of a fee for such building permit to the
building commissioner in the amount of one percent (1%) of the amount of the
performance bond, or one hundred dollars ($100.00), whichever is less. Within
ten (10) days prior to commencement of construction of any public improvements,
the subdivider or the contractor in charge of such construction shall notify
the building commissioner, in writing, of the date upon which such construction
will commence. (Ord., 6-13-1949; amd. 1989 Code)
   E.   Inspection: All public improvements to be made under the provisions of
this chapter shall be inspected during the course of construction by a
competent inspector appointed by the village board. The salary and other costs
in connection with the said inspection shall be paid by the subdivider. (Ord.,
6-13-1949)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 7, chapter 1 of this code.
2 2. See also section
  7-1-11 of this code.
3 3. See section
  7-1-11 of this code.
10-2-6: VARIATIONS:
The building commissioner may approve variations from these requirements in
specific cases which do not affect the general plan or the spirit thereof. All
such variations shall be communicated to the village board in writing with the
reasons therefor before the final approval of the plat by that body. (Ord., 6-
13-1949; amd. 1989 Code)
10-2-7: INTERPRETATION:
In interpreting and applying the provisions of this chapter, such provisions
shall in every instance be held to be the minimum reasonable requirements
adopted for the promotion of public health, safety, comfort, morals and
welfare. (Ord., 6-13-1949)
10-2-8: ENFORCEMENT:
It shall be the duty of the building commissioner to enforce the requirements
of the plan. He may call upon any other department or official of the village
to furnish him with such information or assistance as he may deem necessary for
the observance or enforcement of the plan, and it shall be the duty of such
other departments or officials to furnish such information or assistance
whenever requested. (Ord., 6-13-1949)
10-2-9: PENALTY:
Whoever shall violate any of the provisions of this chapter shall be subject to
a class B penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord., 6-13-1949; amd. 1989 Code)
Each and every violation, and each and every day or part thereof such violation
or failure to comply continues following three (3) days after notification
thereof is sent by registered mail, shall constitute a separate offense. (Ord.
9410, 12-12-1994)
